Markov chain Monte Carlo analysis was run to sample 1,000,000 times with a sampling frequency of 50 and a burn-in of 5,000,000 iterations. We also used CAFE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="De Bie, T., Cristianini, N., Demuth, J. P. &amp; Hahn, M. W. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269–1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2053">57</a></sup> to identify gene families that had undergone expansions or contractions across the maximum likelihood tree.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Resequencing and diversity analysis</h3><p>DNA from 14 <i>L. chinense</i> and 6 <i>L. tulipifera</i> adult plants was extracted, and paired-end libraries with insert sizes of 100–150 bp were sequenced using Illumina technology at BGI. We first called SNPs using BWA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2071">58</a></sup>, GATK<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="DePristo, M. A. et al. A framework for variation discovery and genotyping using next-generation DNA sequencing data. Nat. Genet. 43, 491–498 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2075">59</a></sup> and SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2079">60</a></sup>, then annotated these SNPs using SNPEFF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Cingolani, P. et al. A program for annotating and predicting the effects of single nucleotide polymorphisms, SnpEff: SNPs in the genome of Drosophila melanogaster strain w1118; iso-2; iso-3. Fly (Austin) 6, 80–92 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2084">61</a></sup>, ultimately summarizing them by a customized Perl script.</p><p>The neighbour-joining phylogenetic tree was constructed using TreeBeST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Vilella, A. J. et al. EnsemblCompara GeneTrees: complete, duplication-aware phylogenetic trees in vertebrates. Genome Res. 19, 327–335 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2091">62</a></sup> based on SNPs. Population structure and ancestry information was inferred using FRAPPE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Tang, H., Peng, J., Wang, P. &amp; Risch, N. J. Estimation of individual admixture: analytical and study design considerations. Genet. Epidemiol. 28, 289–301 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2095">63</a></sup> with the best <i>K</i> value determined by ADMIXTURE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Alexander, D. H., Novembre, J. &amp; Lange, K. Fast model-based estimation of ancestry in unrelated individuals. Genome Res. 19, 1655–1664 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2102">64</a></sup> based on a cross-validation test. We additionally performed a principal component analysis using the STRATPCA programme from EIGENSOFT 3.2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Price, A. L. et al. Principal components analysis corrects for stratification in genome-wide association studies. Nat. Genet. 38, 904–909 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2106">65</a></sup>).</p><p>Population genetic parameters, including nucleotide diversity (<i>π</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Nei, M. &amp; Li, W. H. Mathematical model for studying genetic variation in terms of restriction endonucleases. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 76, 5269–5273 (1979)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2116">66</a></sup> and the Watterson estimator (<i>θ</i><sub>w</sub>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Watterson, G. A. On the number of segregating sites in genetical models without recombination. Theor. Popul. Biol. 7, 256–276 (1975)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2124">67</a></sup>, were estimated on the basis of the genotypes of each line at the SNP positions using BioPerl.</p><p>The PSMC model, which was originally applied to human genomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Inference of human population history from individual whole-genome sequences. Nature 475, 493–496 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2131">26</a></sup> and subsequently also applied to plant genomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Amborella Genome, P. The Amborella genome and the evolution of flowering plants. Science 342, 1241089 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2135">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Ibarra-Laclette, E. et al. Architecture and evolution of a minute plant genome. Nature 498, 94–98 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d4932e2138">68</a></sup>, was applied to study the effective population sizes (<i>N</i><sub>e</sub>) of the two <i>Liriodendron</i> species over time.</p><p>See the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#MOESM1">Supplementary Note</a> for additional details.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0323-6#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="code-availability" data-title="Code availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="code-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="code-availability">Code availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="code-availability-content">
              
              <p>The custom Perl script used for summarization of SNP annotation is available from the corresponding author upon request.</p>
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The raw reads and genome assembly have been deposited as a BioProject under accession <a href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/ena/data/view/PRJNA418360">PRJNA418360</a>. The resequencing data for 20 <i>Liriodendron</i> individuals have been deposited as a BioProject under accession <a href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/ena/data/view/PRJNA418361">PRJNA418361</a>.</p>

J.S., J.C., S.Y. and N.L. designed the experiments and coordinated the project. Z.H., P.W., Y.S., Y.Z., Z.W., S.L. and T.C. performed field work and collected samples. X.G., C.Z., P.W, L.Y. and H.X. performed the sequencing experiments. X.G., C.Z., L.X, Qihui Z. and M.S. performed the genome assemblies. Z.H., X.G., C.Z. and L.G. constructed the genetic map. L.X, Q.Z., H.X., X.L. and Y.L. provided RNA-Seq data. X.G., C.Z., L.Y., Q.G. and N.L. performed the gene annotation and genome assembly assessment. J.C., Z.H., X.G., J.Z. and S.Y. performed the genome duplication analysis. Z.H., L.X., L.Y., Y.P. and S.Y. analysed the transposable element insertion. J.C., Z.H., X.G., N.L., S.Y. and J.S. performed the phylogenetic analysis. J.C., Z.H., X.G., T.L., S.Y. and J.S. performed the population genetic structure analysis. J.C., Z.H., S.G., S.Y. and J.S. wrote and edited most of the manuscript. All authors read and approved the final manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
